    1332             : /**
    1333             :  * @brief Explicitly initializes the HIP runtime.
    1334             :  *
    1335             :  * Most HIP APIs implicitly initialize the HIP runtime.
    1336             :  * This API provides control over the timing of the initialization.
    1337             :  */
    1338             : // TODO-ctx - more description on error codes.
    1339             : hipError_t hipInit(unsigned int flags);
    1340             : /**
    1341             :  * @brief Returns the approximate HIP driver version.
    1342             :  *
    1343             :  * @param [out] driverVersion
    1344             :  *
    1345             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    1346             :  *
    1347             :  * @warning The HIP feature set does not correspond to an exact CUDA SDK driver revision.
    1348             :  * This function always set *driverVersion to 4 as an approximation though HIP supports
    1349             :  * some features which were introduced in later CUDA SDK revisions.
    1350             :  * HIP apps code should not rely on the driver revision number here and should
    1351             :  * use arch feature flags to test device capabilities or conditional compilation.
    1352             :  *
    1353             :  * @see hipRuntimeGetVersion
    1354             :  */
    1355             : hipError_t hipDriverGetVersion(int* driverVersion);
    1356             : /**
    1357             :  * @brief Returns the approximate HIP Runtime version.

    1359             :  * @param [out] runtimeVersion
    1360             :  *
    1361             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    1362             :  *
    1363             :  * @warning The version definition of HIP runtime is different from CUDA.
    1364             :  * On AMD platform, the function returns HIP runtime version,
    1365             :  * while on NVIDIA platform, it returns CUDA runtime version.
    1366             :  * And there is no mapping/correlation between HIP version and CUDA version.
    1367             :  *
    1368             :  * @see hipDriverGetVersion
    1369             :  */
    1370             : hipError_t hipRuntimeGetVersion(int* runtimeVersion);

    1450             : /**
    1451             :  *  @defgroup Device Device Management
    1452             :  *  @{
    1453             :  *  This section describes the device management functions of HIP runtime API.
    1454             :  */
    1455             : /**
    1456             :  * @brief Waits on all active streams on current device
    1457             :  *
    1458             :  * When this command is invoked, the host thread gets blocked until all the commands associated
    1459             :  * with streams associated with the device. HIP does not support multiple blocking modes (yet!).
    1460             :  *
    1461             :  * @returns #hipSuccess
    1462             :  *
    1463             :  * @see hipSetDevice, hipDeviceReset
    1464             :  */
    1465             : hipError_t hipDeviceSynchronize(void);
    1466             : /**
    1467             :  * @brief The state of current device is discarded and updated to a fresh state.
    1468             :  *
    1469             :  * Calling this function deletes all streams created, memory allocated, kernels running, events
    1470             :  * created. Make sure that no other thread is using the device or streams, memory, kernels, events
    1471             :  * associated with the current device.
    1472             :  *
    1473             :  * @returns #hipSuccess
    1474             :  *
    1475             :  * @see hipDeviceSynchronize
    1476             :  */
    1477             : hipError_t hipDeviceReset(void);
    1478             : /**
    1479             :  * @brief Set default device to be used for subsequent hip API calls from this thread.
    1480             :  *
    1481             :  * @param[in] deviceId Valid device in range 0...hipGetDeviceCount().
    1482             :  *
    1483             :  * Sets @p device as the default device for the calling host thread.  Valid device id's are 0...
    1484             :  * (hipGetDeviceCount()-1).
    1485             :  *
    1486             :  * Many HIP APIs implicitly use the "default device" :
    1487             :  *
    1488             :  * - Any device memory subsequently allocated from this host thread (using hipMalloc) will be
    1489             :  * allocated on device.
    1490             :  * - Any streams or events created from this host thread will be associated with device.
    1491             :  * - Any kernels launched from this host thread (using hipLaunchKernel) will be executed on device
    1492             :  * (unless a specific stream is specified, in which case the device associated with that stream will
    1493             :  * be used).
    1494             :  *
    1495             :  * This function may be called from any host thread.  Multiple host threads may use the same device.
    1496             :  * This function does no synchronization with the previous or new device, and has very little
    1497             :  * runtime overhead. Applications can use hipSetDevice to quickly switch the default device before
    1498             :  * making a HIP runtime call which uses the default device.
    1499             :  *
    1500             :  * The default device is stored in thread-local-storage for each thread.
    1501             :  * Thread-pool implementations may inherit the default device of the previous thread.  A good
    1502             :  * practice is to always call hipSetDevice at the start of HIP coding sequency to establish a known
    1503             :  * standard device.
    1504             :  *
    1505             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidDevice, #hipErrorDeviceAlreadyInUse
    1506             :  *
    1507             :  * @see hipGetDevice, hipGetDeviceCount
    1508             :  */
    1509             : hipError_t hipSetDevice(int deviceId);
    1510             : /**
    1511             :  * @brief Return the default device id for the calling host thread.
    1512             :  *
    1513             :  * @param [out] device *device is written with the default device
    1514             :  *
    1515             :  * HIP maintains an default device for each thread using thread-local-storage.
    1516             :  * This device is used implicitly for HIP runtime APIs called by this thread.
    1517             :  * hipGetDevice returns in * @p device the default device for the calling host thread.
    1518             :  *
    1519             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidDevice, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    1520             :  *
    1521             :  * @see hipSetDevice, hipGetDevicesizeBytes
    1522             :  */
    1523             : hipError_t hipGetDevice(int* deviceId);
    1524             : /**
    1525             :  * @brief Return number of compute-capable devices.
    1526             :  *
    1527             :  * @param [output] count Returns number of compute-capable devices.
    1528             :  *
    1529             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorNoDevice
    1530             :  *
    1531             :  *
    1532             :  * Returns in @p *count the number of devices that have ability to run compute commands.  If there
    1533             :  * are no such devices, then @ref hipGetDeviceCount will return #hipErrorNoDevice. If 1 or more
    1534             :  * devices can be found, then hipGetDeviceCount returns #hipSuccess.
    1535             :  */
    1536             : hipError_t hipGetDeviceCount(int* count);

    1538             :  * @brief Query for a specific device attribute.

    1556             :  * hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess

    1559             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    1560             :  */
    1561             : hipError_t hipDeviceGetDefaultMemPool(hipMemPool_t* mem_pool, int device);
    1562             : /**
    1563             :  * @brief Sets the current memory pool of a device
    1564             :  *
    1565             :  * The memory pool must be local to the specified device.
    1566             :  * @p hipMallocAsync allocates from the current mempool of the provided stream's device.
    1567             :  * By default, a device's current memory pool is its default memory pool.
    1568             :  *
    1569             :  * @note Use @p hipMallocFromPoolAsync for asynchronous memory allocations from a device
    1570             :  * different than the one the stream runs on.
    1571             :  *

    1573             :  * @param [in] mem_pool Memory pool for update as the current on the specified device
    1574             :  *

    1576             :  *
    1577             :  * @see hipDeviceGetDefaultMemPool, hipMallocAsync, hipMemPoolTrimTo, hipMemPoolGetAttribute,
    1578             :  * hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess

    1580             :  * @warning : This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    1581             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.

    1583             : hipError_t hipDeviceSetMemPool(int device, hipMemPool_t mem_pool);

    1585             :  * @brief Gets the current memory pool for the specified device

    1589             :  * By default the current mempool is the default mempool for a device,
    1590             :  * otherwise the returned pool must have been set with @p hipDeviceSetMemPool.

    1596             :  *

    1599             :  *
    1600             :  * @warning : This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,

    1689             :  * ignored on those architectures.

    1692             : hipError_t hipDeviceSetSharedMemConfig(hipSharedMemConfig config);
    1693             : /**
    1694             :  * @brief The current device behavior is changed according the flags passed.
    1695             :  *
    1696             :  * @param [in] flags
    1697             :  *
    1698             :  * The schedule flags impact how HIP waits for the completion of a command running on a device.
    1699             :  * hipDeviceScheduleSpin         : HIP runtime will actively spin in the thread which submitted the
    1700             :  * work until the command completes.  This offers the lowest latency, but will consume a CPU core
    1701             :  * and may increase power. hipDeviceScheduleYield        : The HIP runtime will yield the CPU to
    1702             :  * system so that other tasks can use it.  This may increase latency to detect the completion but
    1703             :  * will consume less power and is friendlier to other tasks in the system.
    1704             :  * hipDeviceScheduleBlockingSync : On ROCm platform, this is a synonym for hipDeviceScheduleYield.
    1705             :  * hipDeviceScheduleAuto         : Use a hueristic to select between Spin and Yield modes.  If the
    1706             :  * number of HIP contexts is greater than the number of logical processors in the system, use Spin
    1707             :  * scheduling.  Else use Yield scheduling.
    1708             :  *
    1709             :  *
    1710             :  * hipDeviceMapHost              : Allow mapping host memory.  On ROCM, this is always allowed and
    1711             :  * the flag is ignored. hipDeviceLmemResizeToMax      : @warning ROCm silently ignores this flag.
    1712             :  *
    1713             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidDevice, #hipErrorSetOnActiveProcess
    1714             :  *
    1715             :  *
    1716             :  */
    1717             : hipError_t hipSetDeviceFlags(unsigned flags);
    1718             : /**
    1719             :  * @brief Device which matches hipDeviceProp_t is returned

    1734             :  *

    1740             : // TODO: implement IPC apis
    1741             : /**
    1742             :  * @brief Gets an interprocess memory handle for an existing device memory
    1743             :  *          allocation
    1744             :  *
    1745             :  * Takes a pointer to the base of an existing device memory allocation created
    1746             :  * with hipMalloc and exports it for use in another process. This is a
    1747             :  * lightweight operation and may be called multiple times on an allocation
    1748             :  * without adverse effects.
    1749             :  *
    1750             :  * If a region of memory is freed with hipFree and a subsequent call
    1751             :  * to hipMalloc returns memory with the same device address,
    1752             :  * hipIpcGetMemHandle will return a unique handle for the
    1753             :  * new memory.
    1754             :  *
    1755             :  * @param handle - Pointer to user allocated hipIpcMemHandle to return
    1756             :  *                    the handle in.
    1757             :  * @param devPtr - Base pointer to previously allocated device memory
    1758             :  *
    1759             :  * @returns
    1760             :  * hipSuccess,
    1761             :  * hipErrorInvalidHandle,
    1762             :  * hipErrorOutOfMemory,
    1763             :  * hipErrorMapFailed,
    1764             :  *
    1765             :  */
    1766             : hipError_t hipIpcGetMemHandle(hipIpcMemHandle_t* handle, void* devPtr);
    1767             : /**
    1768             :  * @brief Opens an interprocess memory handle exported from another process
    1769             :  *          and returns a device pointer usable in the local process.
    1770             :  *
    1771             :  * Maps memory exported from another process with hipIpcGetMemHandle into
    1772             :  * the current device address space. For contexts on different devices
    1773             :  * hipIpcOpenMemHandle can attempt to enable peer access between the
    1774             :  * devices as if the user called hipDeviceEnablePeerAccess. This behavior is
    1775             :  * controlled by the hipIpcMemLazyEnablePeerAccess flag.
    1776             :  * hipDeviceCanAccessPeer can determine if a mapping is possible.
    1777             :  *
    1778             :  * Contexts that may open hipIpcMemHandles are restricted in the following way.
    1779             :  * hipIpcMemHandles from each device in a given process may only be opened
    1780             :  * by one context per device per other process.
    1781             :  *
    1782             :  * Memory returned from hipIpcOpenMemHandle must be freed with
    1783             :  * hipIpcCloseMemHandle.
    1784             :  *
    1785             :  * Calling hipFree on an exported memory region before calling
    1786             :  * hipIpcCloseMemHandle in the importing context will result in undefined
    1787             :  * behavior.
    1788             :  *
    1789             :  * @param devPtr - Returned device pointer
    1790             :  * @param handle - hipIpcMemHandle to open
    1791             :  * @param flags  - Flags for this operation. Must be specified as hipIpcMemLazyEnablePeerAccess
    1792             :  *
    1793             :  * @returns
    1794             :  * hipSuccess,
    1795             :  * hipErrorMapFailed,
    1796             :  * hipErrorInvalidHandle,
    1797             :  * hipErrorTooManyPeers
    1798             :  *
    1799             :  * @note During multiple processes, using the same memory handle opened by the current context,
    1800             :  * there is no guarantee that the same device poiter will be returned in @p *devPtr.
    1801             :  * This is diffrent from CUDA.
    1802             :  *
    1803             :  */
    1804             : hipError_t hipIpcOpenMemHandle(void** devPtr, hipIpcMemHandle_t handle, unsigned int flags);
    1805             : /**
    1806             :  * @brief Close memory mapped with hipIpcOpenMemHandle
    1807             :  *
    1808             :  * Unmaps memory returnd by hipIpcOpenMemHandle. The original allocation
    1809             :  * in the exporting process as well as imported mappings in other processes
    1810             :  * will be unaffected.
    1811             :  *
    1812             :  * Any resources used to enable peer access will be freed if this is the
    1813             :  * last mapping using them.
    1814             :  *
    1815             :  * @param devPtr - Device pointer returned by hipIpcOpenMemHandle
    1816             :  *
    1817             :  * @returns
    1818             :  * hipSuccess,
    1819             :  * hipErrorMapFailed,
    1820             :  * hipErrorInvalidHandle,
    1821             :  *
    1822             :  */
    1823             : hipError_t hipIpcCloseMemHandle(void* devPtr);
    1824             : 
    1825             : /**
    1826             :  * @brief Gets an opaque interprocess handle for an event.
    1827             :  *
    1828             :  * This opaque handle may be copied into other processes and opened with hipIpcOpenEventHandle.
    1829             :  * Then hipEventRecord, hipEventSynchronize, hipStreamWaitEvent and hipEventQuery may be used in
    1830             :  * either process. Operations on the imported event after the exported event has been freed with hipEventDestroy
    1831             :  * will result in undefined behavior.
    1832             :  *

    1835             :  *

    1839             : hipError_t hipIpcGetEventHandle(hipIpcEventHandle_t* handle, hipEvent_t event);
    1840             : 
    1841             : /**

    1862             : /**
    1863             :  *
    1864             :  *  @defgroup Execution Execution Control
    1865             :  *  @{
    1866             :  *  This section describes the execution control functions of HIP runtime API.

    1869             : /**
    1870             :  * @brief Set attribute for a specific function
    1871             :  *
    1872             :  * @param [in] func;
    1873             :  * @param [in] attr;
    1874             :  * @param [in] value;
    1875             :  *
    1876             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidDeviceFunction, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    1877             :  *
    1878             :  * Note: AMD devices and some Nvidia GPUS do not support shared cache banking, and the hint is
    1879             :  * ignored on those architectures.
    1880             :  *
    1881             :  */
    1882             : hipError_t hipFuncSetAttribute(const void* func, hipFuncAttribute attr, int value);
    1883             : /**

    1889             :  * Note: AMD devices and some Nvidia GPUS do not support reconfigurable cache.  This hint is ignored
    1890             :  * on those architectures.
    1891             :  *
    1892             :  */
    1893             : hipError_t hipFuncSetCacheConfig(const void* func, hipFuncCache_t config);

    2049             :  * @param[in, out] greatestPriority pointer in which value corresponding to greatest priority is returned.
    2050             :  *
    2051             :  * Returns in *leastPriority and *greatestPriority the numerical values that correspond to the least
    2052             :  * and greatest stream priority respectively. Stream priorities follow a convention where lower numbers
    2053             :  * imply greater priorities. The range of meaningful stream priorities is given by
    2054             :  * [*greatestPriority, *leastPriority]. If the user attempts to create a stream with a priority value
    2055             :  * that is outside the the meaningful range as specified by this API, the priority is automatically
    2056             :  * clamped to within the valid range.

    2085             :  *

    2087             :  * host threads are sending work to the stream, the status may change immediately after the function
    2088             :  * is called.  It is typically used for debug.

    2091             :  * hipStreamDestroy
    2092             :  */

    2096             :  *
    2097             :  * @param[in] stream stream identifier.
    2098             :  *
    2099             :  * @return #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidHandle
    2100             :  *
    2101             :  * This command is host-synchronous : the host will block until the specified stream is empty.
    2102             :  *
    2103             :  * This command follows standard null-stream semantics.  Specifically, specifying the null stream
    2104             :  * will cause the command to wait for other streams on the same device to complete all pending
    2105             :  * operations.
    2106             :  *
    2107             :  * This command honors the hipDeviceLaunchBlocking flag, which controls whether the wait is active
    2108             :  * or blocking.
    2109             :  *
    2110             :  * @see hipStreamCreate, hipStreamCreateWithFlags, hipStreamCreateWithPriority, hipStreamWaitEvent, hipStreamDestroy
    2111             :  *
    2112             :  */

    2220             : /**
    2221             :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2222             :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2223             :  *  @defgroup StreamM Stream Memory Operations
    2224             :  *  @{
    2225             :  *  This section describes Stream Memory Wait and Write functions of HIP runtime API.
    2226             :  */
    2227             : /**
    2228             :  * @brief Enqueues a wait command to the stream.[BETA]
    2229             :  *
    2230             :  * @param [in] stream - Stream identifier
    2231             :  * @param [in] ptr    - Pointer to memory object allocated using 'hipMallocSignalMemory' flag
    2232             :  * @param [in] value  - Value to be used in compare operation
    2233             :  * @param [in] flags  - Defines the compare operation, supported values are hipStreamWaitValueGte
    2234             :  * hipStreamWaitValueEq, hipStreamWaitValueAnd and hipStreamWaitValueNor
    2235             :  * @param [in] mask   - Mask to be applied on value at memory before it is compared with value,
    2236             :  * default value is set to enable every bit
    2237             :  *
    2238             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2239             :  *
    2240             :  * Enqueues a wait command to the stream, all operations enqueued  on this stream after this, will
    2241             :  * not execute until the defined wait condition is true.
    2242             :  *
    2243             :  * hipStreamWaitValueGte: waits until *ptr&mask >= value
    2244             :  * hipStreamWaitValueEq : waits until *ptr&mask == value
    2245             :  * hipStreamWaitValueAnd: waits until ((*ptr&mask) & value) != 0
    2246             :  * hipStreamWaitValueNor: waits until ~((*ptr&mask) | (value&mask)) != 0
    2247             :  *
    2248             :  * @note when using 'hipStreamWaitValueNor', mask is applied on both 'value' and '*ptr'.
    2249             :  *
    2250             :  * @note Support for hipStreamWaitValue32 can be queried using 'hipDeviceGetAttribute()' and
    2251             :  * 'hipDeviceAttributeCanUseStreamWaitValue' flag.
    2252             :  *
    2253             :  * @beta This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2254             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2255             :  *
    2256             :  * @see hipExtMallocWithFlags, hipFree, hipStreamWaitValue64, hipStreamWriteValue64,
    2257             :  * hipStreamWriteValue32, hipDeviceGetAttribute
    2258             :  */
    2259             : hipError_t hipStreamWaitValue32(hipStream_t stream, void* ptr, uint32_t value, unsigned int flags,
    2260             :                                 uint32_t mask __dparm(0xFFFFFFFF));
    2261             : /**
    2262             :  * @brief Enqueues a wait command to the stream.[BETA]
    2263             :  *
    2264             :  * @param [in] stream - Stream identifier
    2265             :  * @param [in] ptr    - Pointer to memory object allocated using 'hipMallocSignalMemory' flag
    2266             :  * @param [in] value  - Value to be used in compare operation
    2267             :  * @param [in] flags  - Defines the compare operation, supported values are hipStreamWaitValueGte
    2268             :  * hipStreamWaitValueEq, hipStreamWaitValueAnd and hipStreamWaitValueNor.
    2269             :  * @param [in] mask   - Mask to be applied on value at memory before it is compared with value
    2270             :  * default value is set to enable every bit
    2271             :  *
    2272             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2273             :  *
    2274             :  * Enqueues a wait command to the stream, all operations enqueued  on this stream after this, will
    2275             :  * not execute until the defined wait condition is true.
    2276             :  *
    2277             :  * hipStreamWaitValueGte: waits until *ptr&mask >= value
    2278             :  * hipStreamWaitValueEq : waits until *ptr&mask == value
    2279             :  * hipStreamWaitValueAnd: waits until ((*ptr&mask) & value) != 0
    2280             :  * hipStreamWaitValueNor: waits until ~((*ptr&mask) | (value&mask)) != 0
    2281             :  *
    2282             :  * @note when using 'hipStreamWaitValueNor', mask is applied on both 'value' and '*ptr'.
    2283             :  *
    2284             :  * @note Support for hipStreamWaitValue64 can be queried using 'hipDeviceGetAttribute()' and
    2285             :  * 'hipDeviceAttributeCanUseStreamWaitValue' flag.
    2286             :  *
    2287             :  * @beta This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2288             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2289             :  *
    2290             :  * @see hipExtMallocWithFlags, hipFree, hipStreamWaitValue32, hipStreamWriteValue64,
    2291             :  * hipStreamWriteValue32, hipDeviceGetAttribute
    2292             :  */
    2293             : hipError_t hipStreamWaitValue64(hipStream_t stream, void* ptr, uint64_t value, unsigned int flags,
    2294             :                                 uint64_t mask __dparm(0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF));
    2295             : /**
    2296             :  * @brief Enqueues a write command to the stream.[BETA]
    2297             :  *
    2298             :  * @param [in] stream - Stream identifier
    2299             :  * @param [in] ptr    - Pointer to a GPU accessible memory object
    2300             :  * @param [in] value  - Value to be written
    2301             :  * @param [in] flags  - reserved, ignored for now, will be used in future releases
    2302             :  *
    2303             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2304             :  *
    2305             :  * Enqueues a write command to the stream, write operation is performed after all earlier commands
    2306             :  * on this stream have completed the execution.
    2307             :  *
    2308             :  * @beta This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2309             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2310             :  *
    2311             :  * @see hipExtMallocWithFlags, hipFree, hipStreamWriteValue32, hipStreamWaitValue32,
    2312             :  * hipStreamWaitValue64
    2313             :  */
    2314             : hipError_t hipStreamWriteValue32(hipStream_t stream, void* ptr, uint32_t value, unsigned int flags);
    2315             : /**
    2316             :  * @brief Enqueues a write command to the stream.[BETA]
    2317             :  *
    2318             :  * @param [in] stream - Stream identifier
    2319             :  * @param [in] ptr    - Pointer to a GPU accessible memory object
    2320             :  * @param [in] value  - Value to be written
    2321             :  * @param [in] flags  - reserved, ignored for now, will be used in future releases
    2322             :  *
    2323             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2324             :  *
    2325             :  * Enqueues a write command to the stream, write operation is performed after all earlier commands
    2326             :  * on this stream have completed the execution.
    2327             :  *
    2328             :  * @beta This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2329             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2330             :  *
    2331             :  * @see hipExtMallocWithFlags, hipFree, hipStreamWriteValue32, hipStreamWaitValue32,
    2332             :  * hipStreamWaitValue64
    2333             :  */
    2334             : hipError_t hipStreamWriteValue64(hipStream_t stream, void* ptr, uint64_t value, unsigned int flags);

    2339             : /**
    2340             :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2341             :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2342             :  *  @defgroup Event Event Management
    2343             :  *  @{
    2344             :  *  This section describes the event management functions of HIP runtime API.
    2345             :  */
    2346             : /**
    2347             :  * @brief Create an event with the specified flags
    2348             :  *
    2349             :  * @param[in,out] event Returns the newly created event.
    2350             :  * @param[in] flags     Flags to control event behavior.  Valid values are #hipEventDefault,
    2351             :  #hipEventBlockingSync, #hipEventDisableTiming, #hipEventInterprocess
    2352             :  * #hipEventDefault : Default flag.  The event will use active synchronization and will support
    2353             :  timing.  Blocking synchronization provides lowest possible latency at the expense of dedicating a
    2354             :  CPU to poll on the event.
    2355             :  * #hipEventBlockingSync : The event will use blocking synchronization : if hipEventSynchronize is
    2356             :  called on this event, the thread will block until the event completes.  This can increase latency
    2357             :  for the synchroniation but can result in lower power and more resources for other CPU threads.
    2358             :  * #hipEventDisableTiming : Disable recording of timing information. Events created with this flag
    2359             :  would not record profiling data and provide best performance if used for synchronization.
    2360             :  * #hipEventInterprocess : The event can be used as an interprocess event. hipEventDisableTiming
    2361             :  flag also must be set when hipEventInterprocess flag is set.
    2362             :  *
    2363             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorNotInitialized, #hipErrorInvalidValue,
    2364             :  #hipErrorLaunchFailure, #hipErrorOutOfMemory
    2365             :  *
    2366             :  * @see hipEventCreate, hipEventSynchronize, hipEventDestroy, hipEventElapsedTime
    2367             :  */
    2368             : hipError_t hipEventCreateWithFlags(hipEvent_t* event, unsigned flags);
    2369             : /**
    2370             :  *  Create an event
    2371             :  *
    2372             :  * @param[in,out] event Returns the newly created event.
    2373             :  *
    2374             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorNotInitialized, #hipErrorInvalidValue,
    2375             :  * #hipErrorLaunchFailure, #hipErrorOutOfMemory
    2376             :  *
    2377             :  * @see hipEventCreateWithFlags, hipEventRecord, hipEventQuery, hipEventSynchronize,
    2378             :  * hipEventDestroy, hipEventElapsedTime
    2379             :  */
    2380             : hipError_t hipEventCreate(hipEvent_t* event);
    2381             : /**
    2382             :  * @brief Record an event in the specified stream.
    2383             :  *
    2384             :  * @param[in] event event to record.
    2385             :  * @param[in] stream stream in which to record event.
    2386             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue, #hipErrorNotInitialized,
    2387             :  * #hipErrorInvalidHandle, #hipErrorLaunchFailure
    2388             :  *
    2389             :  * hipEventQuery() or hipEventSynchronize() must be used to determine when the event
    2390             :  * transitions from "recording" (after hipEventRecord() is called) to "recorded"
    2391             :  * (when timestamps are set, if requested).
    2392             :  *
    2393             :  * Events which are recorded in a non-NULL stream will transition to
    2394             :  * from recording to "recorded" state when they reach the head of
    2395             :  * the specified stream, after all previous
    2396             :  * commands in that stream have completed executing.
    2397             :  *
    2398             :  * If hipEventRecord() has been previously called on this event, then this call will overwrite any
    2399             :  * existing state in event.
    2400             :  *
    2401             :  * If this function is called on an event that is currently being recorded, results are undefined
    2402             :  * - either outstanding recording may save state into the event, and the order is not guaranteed.
    2403             :  *
    2404             :  * @see hipEventCreate, hipEventCreateWithFlags, hipEventQuery, hipEventSynchronize,
    2405             :  * hipEventDestroy, hipEventElapsedTime
    2406             :  *
    2407             :  */
    2408             : #ifdef __cplusplus
    2409             : hipError_t hipEventRecord(hipEvent_t event, hipStream_t stream = NULL);
    2410             : #else
    2411             : hipError_t hipEventRecord(hipEvent_t event, hipStream_t stream);
    2412             : #endif
    2413             : /**
    2414             :  *  @brief Destroy the specified event.
    2415             :  *
    2416             :  *  @param[in] event Event to destroy.
    2417             :  *  @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorNotInitialized, #hipErrorInvalidValue,
    2418             :  * #hipErrorLaunchFailure
    2419             :  *
    2420             :  *  Releases memory associated with the event.  If the event is recording but has not completed
    2421             :  * recording when hipEventDestroy() is called, the function will return immediately and the
    2422             :  * completion_future resources will be released later, when the hipDevice is synchronized.
    2423             :  *
    2424             :  * @see hipEventCreate, hipEventCreateWithFlags, hipEventQuery, hipEventSynchronize, hipEventRecord,
    2425             :  * hipEventElapsedTime
    2426             :  *
    2427             :  * @returns #hipSuccess
    2428             :  */
    2429             : hipError_t hipEventDestroy(hipEvent_t event);
    2430             : /**
    2431             :  *  @brief Wait for an event to complete.
    2432             :  *
    2433             :  *  This function will block until the event is ready, waiting for all previous work in the stream
    2434             :  * specified when event was recorded with hipEventRecord().
    2435             :  *
    2436             :  *  If hipEventRecord() has not been called on @p event, this function returns immediately.
    2437             :  *
    2438             :  *  TODO-hip- This function needs to support hipEventBlockingSync parameter.
    2439             :  *
    2440             :  *  @param[in] event Event on which to wait.
    2441             :  *  @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue, #hipErrorNotInitialized,
    2442             :  * #hipErrorInvalidHandle, #hipErrorLaunchFailure
    2443             :  *
    2444             :  *  @see hipEventCreate, hipEventCreateWithFlags, hipEventQuery, hipEventDestroy, hipEventRecord,
    2445             :  * hipEventElapsedTime
    2446             :  */
    2447             : hipError_t hipEventSynchronize(hipEvent_t event);
    2448             : /**
    2449             :  * @brief Return the elapsed time between two events.
    2450             :  *
    2451             :  * @param[out] ms : Return time between start and stop in ms.
    2452             :  * @param[in]   start : Start event.
    2453             :  * @param[in]   stop  : Stop event.
    2454             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue, #hipErrorNotReady, #hipErrorInvalidHandle,
    2455             :  * #hipErrorNotInitialized, #hipErrorLaunchFailure
    2456             :  *
    2457             :  * Computes the elapsed time between two events. Time is computed in ms, with
    2458             :  * a resolution of approximately 1 us.
    2459             :  *
    2460             :  * Events which are recorded in a NULL stream will block until all commands
    2461             :  * on all other streams complete execution, and then record the timestamp.
    2462             :  *
    2463             :  * Events which are recorded in a non-NULL stream will record their timestamp
    2464             :  * when they reach the head of the specified stream, after all previous
    2465             :  * commands in that stream have completed executing.  Thus the time that
    2466             :  * the event recorded may be significantly after the host calls hipEventRecord().
    2467             :  *
    2468             :  * If hipEventRecord() has not been called on either event, then #hipErrorInvalidHandle is
    2469             :  * returned. If hipEventRecord() has been called on both events, but the timestamp has not yet been
    2470             :  * recorded on one or both events (that is, hipEventQuery() would return #hipErrorNotReady on at
    2471             :  * least one of the events), then #hipErrorNotReady is returned.
    2472             :  *
    2473             :  * @see hipEventCreate, hipEventCreateWithFlags, hipEventQuery, hipEventDestroy, hipEventRecord,
    2474             :  * hipEventSynchronize
    2475             :  */
    2476             : hipError_t hipEventElapsedTime(float* ms, hipEvent_t start, hipEvent_t stop);
    2477             : /**
    2478             :  * @brief Query event status
    2479             :  *
    2480             :  * @param[in] event Event to query.
    2481             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorNotReady, #hipErrorInvalidHandle, #hipErrorInvalidValue,
    2482             :  * #hipErrorNotInitialized, #hipErrorLaunchFailure
    2483             :  *
    2484             :  * Query the status of the specified event.  This function will return #hipSuccess if all
    2485             :  * commands in the appropriate stream (specified to hipEventRecord()) have completed.  If that work
    2486             :  * has not completed, or if hipEventRecord() was not called on the event, then #hipErrorNotReady is
    2487             :  * returned.
    2488             :  *
    2489             :  * @see hipEventCreate, hipEventCreateWithFlags, hipEventRecord, hipEventDestroy,
    2490             :  * hipEventSynchronize, hipEventElapsedTime
    2491             :  */
    2492             : hipError_t hipEventQuery(hipEvent_t event);

    2783             :  *                          where the result of each attribute query will be written to
    2784             :  * @param [in] data_sizes   an array, containing the sizes of each result
    2785             :  * @param [in] attributes   the attribute to query
    2786             :  * @param [in] num_attributes  an array of attributes to query (numAttributes and the number
    2787             :  *                          of attributes in this array should match)
    2788             :  * @param [in] dev_ptr      start of the range to query
    2789             :  * @param [in] count        size of the range to query
    2790             :  *
    2791             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2792             :  */
    2793             : hipError_t hipMemRangeGetAttributes(void** data,
    2794             :                                     size_t* data_sizes,
    2795             :                                     hipMemRangeAttribute* attributes,
    2796             :                                     size_t num_attributes,
    2797             :                                     const void* dev_ptr,
    2798             :                                     size_t count);
    2799             : /**
    2800             :  * @brief Attach memory to a stream asynchronously in HIP.
    2801             :  *
    2802             :  * @param [in] stream     - stream in which to enqueue the attach operation
    2803             :  * @param [in] dev_ptr    - pointer to memory (must be a pointer to managed memory or
    2804             :  *                          to a valid host-accessible region of system-allocated memory)
    2805             :  * @param [in] length     - length of memory (defaults to zero)
    2806             :  * @param [in] flags      - must be one of hipMemAttachGlobal, hipMemAttachHost or
    2807             :  *                          hipMemAttachSingle (defaults to hipMemAttachSingle)
    2808             :  *
    2809             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2810             :  */
    2811             : hipError_t hipStreamAttachMemAsync(hipStream_t stream,
    2812             :                                    void* dev_ptr,
    2813             :                                    size_t length __dparm(0),
    2814             :                                    unsigned int flags __dparm(hipMemAttachSingle));
    2815             : // end doxygen Managed Memory
    2816             : /**
    2817             :  * @}
    2818             :  */
    2819             : 
    2820             : /**
    2821             :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2822             :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2823             :  * @addtogroup StreamO Ordered Memory Allocator
    2824             :  * @{
    2825             :  * @ingroup Memory
    2826             :  * This section describes Stream Ordered Memory Allocator functions of HIP runtime API.
    2827             :  *
    2828             :  * The asynchronous allocator allows the user to allocate and free in stream order.
    2829             :  * All asynchronous accesses of the allocation must happen between the stream executions of
    2830             :  * the allocation and the free. If the memory is accessed outside of the promised stream order,
    2831             :  * a use before allocation / use after free error  will cause undefined behavior.
    2832             :  *
    2833             :  * The allocator is free to reallocate the memory as long as it can guarantee that compliant memory
    2834             :  * accesses will not overlap temporally. The allocator may refer to internal stream ordering as well
    2835             :  * as inter-stream dependencies (such as HIP events and null stream dependencies) when establishing
    2836             :  * the temporal guarantee. The allocator may also insert inter-stream dependencies to establish
    2837             :  * the temporal guarantee.  Whether or not a device supports the integrated stream ordered memory
    2838             :  * allocator may be queried by calling @p hipDeviceGetAttribute with the device attribute
    2839             :  * @p hipDeviceAttributeMemoryPoolsSupported
    2840             :  */
    2841             : 
    2842             : /**
    2843             :  * @brief Allocates memory with stream ordered semantics
    2844             :  *
    2845             :  * Inserts a memory allocation operation into @p stream.
    2846             :  * A pointer to the allocated memory is returned immediately in *dptr.
    2847             :  * The allocation must not be accessed until the the allocation operation completes.
    2848             :  * The allocation comes from the memory pool associated with the stream's device.
    2849             :  *
    2850             :  * @note The default memory pool of a device contains device memory from that device.
    2851             :  * @note Basic stream ordering allows future work submitted into the same stream to use the allocation.
    2852             :  * Stream query, stream synchronize, and HIP events can be used to guarantee that the allocation
    2853             :  * operation completes before work submitted in a separate stream runs.
    2854             :  * @note During stream capture, this function results in the creation of an allocation node. In this case,
    2855             :  * the allocation is owned by the graph instead of the memory pool. The memory pool's properties
    2856             :  * are used to set the node's creation parameters.
    2857             :  *
    2858             :  * @param [out] dev_ptr  Returned device pointer of memory allocation
    2859             :  * @param [in] size      Number of bytes to allocate
    2860             :  * @param [in] stream    The stream establishing the stream ordering contract and
    2861             :  *                       the memory pool to allocate from
    2862             :  *
    2863             :  * @return #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue, #hipErrorNotSupported, #hipErrorOutOfMemory
    2864             :  *
    2865             :  * @see hipMallocFromPoolAsync, hipFreeAsync, hipMemPoolTrimTo, hipMemPoolGetAttribute,
    2866             :  * hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess
    2867             :  *
    2868             :  * @warning : This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2869             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2870             :  */
    2871             : hipError_t hipMallocAsync(void** dev_ptr, size_t size, hipStream_t stream);
    2872             : /**
    2873             :  * @brief Frees memory with stream ordered semantics
    2874             :  *
    2875             :  * Inserts a free operation into @p stream.
    2876             :  * The allocation must not be used after stream execution reaches the free.
    2877             :  * After this API returns, accessing the memory from any subsequent work launched on the GPU
    2878             :  * or querying its pointer attributes results in undefined behavior.
    2879             :  *
    2880             :  * @note During stream capture, this function results in the creation of a free node and
    2881             :  * must therefore be passed the address of a graph allocation.
    2882             :  *
    2883             :  * @param [in] dev_ptr Pointer to device memory to free
    2884             :  * @param [in] stream  The stream, where the destruciton will occur according to the execution order
    2885             :  *
    2886             :  * @returns hipSuccess, hipErrorInvalidValue, hipErrorNotSupported
    2887             :  *
    2888             :  * @see hipMallocFromPoolAsync, hipMallocAsync, hipMemPoolTrimTo, hipMemPoolGetAttribute,
    2889             :  * hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess
    2890             :  *
    2891             :  * @warning : This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2892             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2893             :  */
    2894             : hipError_t hipFreeAsync(void* dev_ptr, hipStream_t stream);
    2895             : /**
    2896             :  * @brief Releases freed memory back to the OS
    2897             :  *
    2898             :  * Releases memory back to the OS until the pool contains fewer than @p min_bytes_to_keep
    2899             :  * reserved bytes, or there is no more memory that the allocator can safely release.
    2900             :  * The allocator cannot release OS allocations that back outstanding asynchronous allocations.
    2901             :  * The OS allocations may happen at different granularity from the user allocations.
    2902             :  *
    2903             :  * @note: Allocations that have not been freed count as outstanding.
    2904             :  * @note: Allocations that have been asynchronously freed but whose completion has
    2905             :  * not been observed on the host (eg. by a synchronize) can count as outstanding.
    2906             :  *
    2907             :  * @param[in] mem_pool          The memory pool to trim allocations
    2908             :  * @param[in] min_bytes_to_hold If the pool has less than min_bytes_to_hold reserved,
    2909             :  * then the TrimTo operation is a no-op.  Otherwise the memory pool will contain
    2910             :  * at least min_bytes_to_hold bytes reserved after the operation.
    2911             :  *
    2912             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2913             :  *
    2914             :  * @see hipMallocFromPoolAsync, hipMallocAsync, hipFreeAsync, hipMemPoolGetAttribute,
    2915             :  * hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess
    2916             :  *
    2917             :  * @warning : This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2918             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2919             :  */
    2920             : hipError_t hipMemPoolTrimTo(hipMemPool_t mem_pool, size_t min_bytes_to_hold);
    2921             : /**
    2922             :  * @brief Sets attributes of a memory pool
    2923             :  *
    2924             :  * Supported attributes are:
    2925             :  * - @p hipMemPoolAttrReleaseThreshold: (value type = cuuint64_t)
    2926             :  *                                  Amount of reserved memory in bytes to hold onto before trying
    2927             :  *                                  to release memory back to the OS. When more than the release
    2928             :  *                                  threshold bytes of memory are held by the memory pool, the
    2929             :  *                                  allocator will try to release memory back to the OS on the
    2930             :  *                                  next call to stream, event or context synchronize. (default 0)
    2931             :  * - @p hipMemPoolReuseFollowEventDependencies: (value type = int)
    2932             :  *                                  Allow @p hipMallocAsync to use memory asynchronously freed
    2933             :  *                                  in another stream as long as a stream ordering dependency
    2934             :  *                                  of the allocating stream on the free action exists.
    2935             :  *                                  HIP events and null stream interactions can create the required
    2936             :  *                                  stream ordered dependencies. (default enabled)
    2937             :  * - @p hipMemPoolReuseAllowOpportunistic: (value type = int)
    2938             :  *                                  Allow reuse of already completed frees when there is no dependency
    2939             :  *                                  between the free and allocation. (default enabled)
    2940             :  * - @p hipMemPoolReuseAllowInternalDependencies: (value type = int)
    2941             :  *                                  Allow @p hipMallocAsync to insert new stream dependencies
    2942             :  *                                  in order to establish the stream ordering required to reuse
    2943             :  *                                  a piece of memory released by @p hipFreeAsync (default enabled).
    2944             :  *
    2945             :  * @param [in] mem_pool The memory pool to modify
    2946             :  * @param [in] attr     The attribute to modify
    2947             :  * @param [in] value    Pointer to the value to assign
    2948             :  *
    2949             :  * @returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2950             :  *
    2951             :  * @see hipMallocFromPoolAsync, hipMallocAsync, hipFreeAsync, hipMemPoolGetAttribute,
    2952             :  * hipMemPoolTrimTo, hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess
    2953             :  *
    2954             :  * @warning : This API is marked as beta, meaning, while this is feature complete,
    2955             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2956             :  */
    2957             : hipError_t hipMemPoolSetAttribute(hipMemPool_t mem_pool, hipMemPoolAttr attr, void* value);
    2958             : /**
    2959             :  * @brief Gets attributes of a memory pool
    2960             :  *
    2961             :  * Supported attributes are:
    2962             :  * - @p hipMemPoolAttrReleaseThreshold: (value type = cuuint64_t)
    2963             :  *                                  Amount of reserved memory in bytes to hold onto before trying
    2964             :  *                                  to release memory back to the OS. When more than the release
    2965             :  *                                  threshold bytes of memory are held by the memory pool, the
    2966             :  *                                  allocator will try to release memory back to the OS on the
    2967             :  *                                  next call to stream, event or context synchronize. (default 0)
    2968             :  * - @p hipMemPoolReuseFollowEventDependencies: (value type = int)
    2969             :  *                                  Allow @p hipMallocAsync to use memory asynchronously freed
    2970             :  *                                  in another stream as long as a stream ordering dependency
    2971             :  *                                  of the allocating stream on the free action exists.
    2972             :  *                                  HIP events and null stream interactions can create the required
    2973             :  *                                  stream ordered dependencies. (default enabled)
    2974             :  * - @p hipMemPoolReuseAllowOpportunistic: (value type = int)
    2975             :  *                                  Allow reuse of already completed frees when there is no dependency
    2976             :  *                                  between the free and allocation. (default enabled)
    2977             :  * - @p hipMemPoolReuseAllowInternalDependencies: (value type = int)
    2978             :  *                                  Allow @p hipMallocAsync to insert new stream dependencies
    2979             :  *                                  in order to establish the stream ordering required to reuse
    2980             :  *                                  a piece of memory released by @p hipFreeAsync (default enabled).

    2982             :  * @param [in] mem_pool The memory pool to get attributes of

    2984             :  * @param [in] value    Retrieved value
    2985             :  *
    2986             :  * @returns  #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidValue
    2987             :  *
    2988             :  * @see hipMallocFromPoolAsync, hipMallocAsync, hipFreeAsync,
    2989             :  * hipMemPoolTrimTo, hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess
    2990             :  *

    2992             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    2993             :  */
    2994             : hipError_t hipMemPoolGetAttribute(hipMemPool_t mem_pool, hipMemPoolAttr attr, void* value);
    2995             : /**
    2996             :  * @brief Controls visibility of the specified pool between devices

    3029             : /**
    3030             :  * @brief Creates a memory pool

    3057             :  * resources associated with the pool will be released automatically

    3073             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.

    3076             : /**
    3077             :  * @brief Allocates memory from a specified pool with stream ordered semantics.
    3078             :  *
    3079             :  * Inserts an allocation operation into @p stream.
    3080             :  * A pointer to the allocated memory is returned immediately in @p dev_ptr.
    3081             :  * The allocation must not be accessed until the the allocation operation completes.
    3082             :  * The allocation comes from the specified memory pool.
    3083             :  *
    3084             :  * @note The specified memory pool may be from a device different than that of the specified @p stream.
    3085             :  *
    3086             :  * Basic stream ordering allows future work submitted into the same stream to use the allocation.
    3087             :  * Stream query, stream synchronize, and HIP events can be used to guarantee that the allocation
    3088             :  * operation completes before work submitted in a separate stream runs.
    3089             :  *
    3090             :  * @note During stream capture, this function results in the creation of an allocation node. In this case,
    3091             :  * the allocation is owned by the graph instead of the memory pool. The memory pool's properties
    3092             :  * are used to set the node's creation parameters.
    3093             :  *

    3095             :  * @param [in] size     Number of bytes to allocate

    3097             :  * @param [in] stream   The stream establishing the stream ordering semantic
    3098             :  *

    3100             :  *
    3101             :  * @see hipMallocAsync, hipFreeAsync, hipMemPoolGetAttribute, hipMemPoolCreate
    3102             :  * hipMemPoolTrimTo, hipDeviceSetMemPool, hipMemPoolSetAttribute, hipMemPoolSetAccess, hipMemPoolGetAccess,
    3103             :  *

    3105             :  * it is still open to changes and may have outstanding issues.
    3106             :  */

    3108             : /**
    3109             :  * @brief Exports a memory pool to the requested handle type.
    3110             :  *
    3111             :  * Given an IPC capable mempool, create an OS handle to share the pool with another process.
    3112             :  * A recipient process can convert the shareable handle into a mempool with @p hipMemPoolImportFromShareableHandle.
    3113             :  * Individual pointers can then be shared with the @p hipMemPoolExportPointer and @p hipMemPoolImportPointer APIs.
    3114             :  * The implementation of what the shareable handle is and how it can be transferred is defined by the requested
    3115             :  * handle type.
    3116             :  *
    3117             :  * @note: To create an IPC capable mempool, create a mempool with a @p hipMemAllocationHandleType other
    3118             :  * than @p hipMemHandleTypeNone.
    3119             :  *

    3121             :  * @param [in] mem_pool       Pool to export

    3123             :  * @param [in] flags          Must be 0

    3141             :  *

    3143             :  * As such imported memory pools may not be used in @p hipDeviceSetMemPool

    3164             :  * @brief Export data to share a memory pool allocation between processes.

    3167             :  * The recipient process can import the allocation with the @p hipMemPoolImportPointer api.
    3168             :  * The data is not a handle and may be shared through any IPC mechanism.

    3181             : /**
    3182             :  * @brief Import a memory pool allocation from another process.
    3183             :  *
    3184             :  * Returns in @p dev_ptr a pointer to the imported memory.
    3185             :  * The imported memory must not be accessed before the allocation operation completes
    3186             :  * in the exporting process. The imported memory must be freed from all importing processes before
    3187             :  * being freed in the exporting process. The pointer may be freed with @p hipFree
    3188             :  * or @p hipFreeAsync. If @p hipFreeAsync is used, the free must be completed
    3189             :  * on the importing process before the free operation on the exporting process.
    3190             :  *
    3191             :  * @note The @p hipFreeAsync api may be used in the exporting process before
    3192             :  * the @p hipFreeAsync operation completes in its stream as long as the
    3193             :  * @p hipFreeAsync in the exporting process specifies a stream with
    3194             :  * a stream dependency on the importing process's @p hipFreeAsync.
    3195             :  *

    3253             : /**
    3254             :  *  @brief Register host memory so it can be accessed from the current device.
    3255             :  *
    3256             :  *  @param[out] hostPtr Pointer to host memory to be registered.
    3257             :  *  @param[in] sizeBytes size of the host memory
    3258             :  *  @param[in] flags.  See below.
    3259             :  *
    3260             :  *  Flags:
    3261             :  *  - #hipHostRegisterDefault   Memory is Mapped and Portable
    3262             :  *  - #hipHostRegisterPortable  Memory is considered registered by all contexts.  HIP only supports
    3263             :  * one context so this is always assumed true.
    3264             :  *  - #hipHostRegisterMapped    Map the allocation into the address space for the current device.
    3265             :  * The device pointer can be obtained with #hipHostGetDevicePointer.
    3266             :  *
    3267             :  *
    3268             :  *  After registering the memory, use #hipHostGetDevicePointer to obtain the mapped device pointer.
    3269             :  *  On many systems, the mapped device pointer will have a different value than the mapped host
    3270             :  * pointer.  Applications must use the device pointer in device code, and the host pointer in device
    3271             :  * code.
    3272             :  *
    3273             :  *  On some systems, registered memory is pinned.  On some systems, registered memory may not be
    3274             :  * actually be pinned but uses OS or hardware facilities to all GPU access to the host memory.
    3275             :  *
    3276             :  *  Developers are strongly encouraged to register memory blocks which are aligned to the host
    3277             :  * cache-line size. (typically 64-bytes but can be obtains from the CPUID instruction).
    3278             :  *
    3279             :  *  If registering non-aligned pointers, the application must take care when register pointers from
    3280             :  * the same cache line on different devices.  HIP's coarse-grained synchronization model does not
    3281             :  * guarantee correct results if different devices write to different parts of the same cache block -
    3282             :  * typically one of the writes will "win" and overwrite data from the other registered memory
    3283             :  * region.
    3284             :  *
    3285             :  *  @return #hipSuccess, #hipErrorOutOfMemory
    3286             :  *
    3287             :  *  @see hipHostUnregister, hipHostGetFlags, hipHostGetDevicePointer
    3288             :  */
    3289             : hipError_t hipHostRegister(void* hostPtr, size_t sizeBytes, unsigned int flags);
    3290             : /**
    3291             :  *  @brief Un-register host pointer
    3292             :  *

    3294             :  *  @return Error code
    3295             :  *
    3296             :  *  @see hipHostRegister
    3297             :  */
    3298             : hipError_t hipHostUnregister(void* hostPtr);

    3638             :  *
    3639             :  *  @warning on HCC hipMemcpyAsync does not support overlapped H2D and D2H copies.
    3640             :  *  For hipMemcpy, the copy is always performed by the device associated with the specified stream.
    3641             :  *
    3642             :  *  For multi-gpu or peer-to-peer configurations, it is recommended to use a stream which is a
    3643             :  * attached to the device where the src data is physically located. For optimal peer-to-peer copies,
    3644             :  * the copy device must be able to access the src and dst pointers (by calling
    3645             :  * hipDeviceEnablePeerAccess with copy agent as the current device and src/dest as the peerDevice
    3646             :  * argument.  if this is not done, the hipMemcpy will still work, but will perform the copy using a
    3647             :  * staging buffer on the host.
    3648             :  *

    4157             :  * @brief Determine if a device can access a peer's memory.
    4158             :  *
    4159             :  * @param [out] canAccessPeer Returns the peer access capability (0 or 1)
    4160             :  * @param [in] device - device from where memory may be accessed.
    4161             :  * @param [in] peerDevice - device where memory is physically located
    4162             :  *
    4163             :  * Returns "1" in @p canAccessPeer if the specified @p device is capable
    4164             :  * of directly accessing memory physically located on peerDevice , or "0" if not.
    4165             :  *
    4166             :  * Returns "0" in @p canAccessPeer if deviceId == peerDeviceId, and both are valid devices : a
    4167             :  * device is not a peer of itself.
    4168             :  *
    4169             :  * @returns #hipSuccess,
    4170             :  * @returns #hipErrorInvalidDevice if deviceId or peerDeviceId are not valid devices
    4171             :  */
    4172             : hipError_t hipDeviceCanAccessPeer(int* canAccessPeer, int deviceId, int peerDeviceId);
    4173             : /**
    4174             :  * @brief Enable direct access from current device's virtual address space to memory allocations
    4175             :  * physically located on a peer device.
    4176             :  *
    4177             :  * Memory which already allocated on peer device will be mapped into the address space of the
    4178             :  * current device.  In addition, all future memory allocations on peerDeviceId will be mapped into
    4179             :  * the address space of the current device when the memory is allocated. The peer memory remains
    4180             :  * accessible from the current device until a call to hipDeviceDisablePeerAccess or hipDeviceReset.
    4181             :  *
    4182             :  *
    4183             :  * @param [in] peerDeviceId
    4184             :  * @param [in] flags
    4185             :  *
    4186             :  * Returns #hipSuccess, #hipErrorInvalidDevice, #hipErrorInvalidValue,
    4187             :  * @returns #hipErrorPeerAccessAlreadyEnabled if peer access is already enabled for this device.
    4188             :  */
    4189             : hipError_t hipDeviceEnablePeerAccess(int peerDeviceId, unsigned int flags);
    4190             : /**
    4191             :  * @brief Disable direct access from current device's virtual address space to memory allocations
    4192             :  * physically located on a peer device.

    4195             :  * enabled from the current device.
    4196             :  *
